<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">355.9.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;Unit,&quot; &quot;gear,&quot; and &quot;rune&quot; refer to objects on the Board unless specified otherwise.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">355.9.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;Spell&quot; and &quot;ability&quot; refer to objects on the Chain unless specified otherwise.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">355.9.a.3.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;Facedown card&quot; refers to a card in a Facedown Zone unless specified otherwise.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">355.9.a.4.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;Legend&quot; refers to a legend in the Legend Zone.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">355.9.a.5.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;Chosen Champion&quot; and &quot;unit in the Champion Zone&quot; refer to a unit in the Champion Zone unless specified otherwise.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.9.b.</div><div class="rule-text">It meets all targeting restrictions. e.g., A unit is a valid target for a spell that refers to a &quot;unit at a battlefield,&quot; &quot;enemy unit,&quot; &quot;unit you control,&quot; or &quot;unit with Might 4 or greater&quot; only if it meets the appropriate criteria.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.9.c.</div><div class="rule-text">It is not the spell or ability itself. e.g., A spell that says &quot;Counter a spell&quot; cannot target itself. e.g., An ability of a permanent can target that permanent, because abilities and their sources are separate objects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">355.10.</div><div class="rule-text">A game object, player, or zone mentioned in the text of a spell, activated ability, or triggered ability is a target UNLESS any of the following are true:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.10.a.</div><div class="rule-text">It is in a zone whose information status is not Public. e.g., &quot;Ready a legend&quot; targets a legend, because the Legend Zone is Public. e.g., &quot;Return a unit from your trash to your hand&quot; targets a unit card in your trash, because your trash is Public. e.g., &quot;You may play a unit from your hand, ignoring its costs&quot; does not target a unit card in your hand, because your hand is not a public zone.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">355.10.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Public zones are Battlefield Zones, Bases, Trashes, Legend Zones, Champion Zones, and Facedown Zones.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.10.b.</div><div class="rule-text">It is included only as part of a targeting restriction for another choice. e.g., &quot;Kill a unit at a battlefield&quot; targets a unit, but not a battlefield, because the units are targets and &quot;at a battlefield&quot; is a restriction. e.g., &quot;Kill all units at a battlefield&quot; targets a battlefield, but not any units.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.10.c.</div><div class="rule-text">It is included only as part of a cost, trigger condition, or replacement effect. e.g., &quot;As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit&quot; doesn&#x27;t target anything. e.g., &quot;When a friendly unit dies, kill a gear&quot; targets a gear, but not a friendly unit. e.g., &quot;When you play me, the next time a friendly unit would die this turn, return it to your hand instead&quot; doesn&#x27;t target anything. The replacement effect applies when any friendly unit dies. e.g., &quot;Choose a friendly unit. The next time it would die this turn, return it to your hand instead&quot; targets a friendly unit, because &quot;choose a friendly unit&quot; is not part of the replacement effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">355.10.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">This includes costs within instructions, identified by phrases like &quot;[do X] to [do Y].&quot; The cost within that instruction is &quot;[do X].&quot; e.g., &quot;When I hold, you may kill another friendly unit here to draw 1&quot; does not target anything. e.g., &quot;When you play me, you may spend a buff to move a friendly unit&quot; targets the friendly unit, but not the buff.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.10.d.</div><div class="rule-text">It is programmatically selected based on its characteristics rather than chosen by the spell or ability&#x27;s controller. e.g., &quot;Kill all units at a battlefield&quot; targets a battlefield, but does not target any units. e.g., &quot;Kill all units at battlefields&quot; doesn&#x27;t target anything. e.g., &quot;Destroy a unit. Its controller draws 2 cards&quot; targets the unit, but not its controller. e.g., &quot;Ready your legend&quot; doesn&#x27;t target anything, because you can only have one legend. e.g., &quot;Ready a friendly legend&quot; targets a legend, because in a 2v2 game there are two friendly legends. e.g., &quot;Recycle all cards in your trash&quot; doesn&#x27;t target anything, because it affects all cards and you only have one trash.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">355.10.d.1.</div><div class="rule-text">This exception applies solely to objects for which no choice is ever possible.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">355.10.d.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This exception does not apply to objects that are the only valid choice at the moment a spell or ability is placed on the chain, but which would require a choice under other circumstances. e.g., &quot;Kill a unit at a battlefield&quot; always targets a unit, even if that unit is the only unit currently at a battlefield.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.10.e.</div><div class="rule-text">It is part of a set of objects chosen in whole or in part by other players. e.g., &quot;Each player kills a unit they control&quot; does not target. Each player, including the one who played the spell, chooses a unit to kill as the spell or ability resolves.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.10.f.</div><div class="rule-text">It is identified in an instruction that a player &quot;must&quot; complete. e.g., &quot;You must recycle one of your runes&quot; doesn&#x27;t target anything. You choose from among your runes as the spell or ability resolves. e.g., &quot;Recycle a rune you control&quot; targets a rune. You choose a rune you control as you put the spell or ability on the chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">355.11.</div><div class="rule-text">Some cards identify a group of Targets with Targeting Requirements that must be met by the group as a whole.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.11.a.</div><div class="rule-text">As they&#x27;re finalized on the chain, such cards can choose any group of valid targets that collectively fulfill the targeting restriction.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.11.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If the group of targets no longer collectively fulfill the targeting restriction as the spell or ability resolves, that spell or ability&#x27;s controller can choose a subset of the original targets that fulfills the targeting requirement for the spell or ability to affect. Example: A player plays Fox-Fire, a spell that says in part &quot;Kill any number of units at a battlefield with total Might 4 or less.&quot; That player chooses four 1 [M] Recruit tokens at a single battlefield. As a Reaction, another player gives two of those Recruits +1 [M], so the Recruits&#x27; Mights are 1, 1, 2, and 2. Then Fox-Fire resolves. The Recruits no longer have total Might 4 or less, so Fox-Fire&#x27;s controller must choose a legal subset of the original targets to affect. They could choose to kill the two 2 [M] Recruits, or the two 1 [M] Recruits plus one 2 [M] Recruit. The units they choose are Fox-Fire&#x27;s remaining legal targets. They can&#x27;t choose to affect units at the same battlefield that weren&#x27;t initially chosen as targets. They can, however, choose to affect units that were initially chosen as targets that left the chosen battlefield before Fox-Fire resolved as long as those units are all located at the same battlefield.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">355.12.</div><div class="rule-text">If a spell specifies that a player may perform a Game Action on some number of Game Objects , then all choices are considered targeted and chosen independently of the decision to perform the Game Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">355.13.</div><div class="rule-text">If a card specifies that a player chooses &quot;any number&quot; or &quot;up to&quot; some number of Game Objects to be affected, they may choose any number of available targets, including zero. If they choose zero, the spell or ability can be played without any targets.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">355.14.</div><div class="rule-text">Splitting</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.14.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If a card specifies that an amount of damage may be split among some number of Units , then each Unit chosen is Targeted.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.14.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The Targets are chosen when the spell or ability is finalized on the chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.14.c.</div><div class="rule-text">A number of Targets can only be chosen up to, and not exceeding, the initial amount of damage available when the spell is played. Example: A player playing a spell that instructs them to &quot;Split 5 damage&quot; may only choose up to 5 units, but may choose fewer.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.14.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Each Target is valid, and contributes to Chosen triggers individually.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.14.e.</div><div class="rule-text">The choice of how much damage is divided across the split is not decided until the resolution of the spell or ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.14.f.</div><div class="rule-text">Each Target must receive a valid amount of damage.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.14.g.</div><div class="rule-text">Valid damage is a positive integer amount, greater than or equal to 1 damage. See rule 417. Deal for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.14.h.</div><div class="rule-text">If, at resolution of the spell or effect, there are more Targets than available damage to divide, then the player who controls the effect dealing damage determines which Targets cease being Targets.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">355.14.i.</div><div class="rule-text">Any costs that were paid, or effects that were triggered as a result of those Game Objects being chosen as Targets remain in effect, paid, or otherwise triggered.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">355.15.</div><div class="rule-text">These choices cannot be changed after this step.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">355.16.</div><div class="rule-text">A player may not make choices during this step that will deterministically result in illegal choices or actions later in this process unless they have no choice. Example: A player plays a card which reads &quot;as an additional cost to play this, kill the unit you control with the most Might. Give a friendly unit +[M] equal to the killed unit&#x27;s Might this turn. Predict 2.&quot; They cannot choose to target their unit with the highest Might during this step of finalization.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">355.17.</div><div class="rule-text">If a spell or ability requires one or more players to make choices that are not outlined in this section, they are made on resolution.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">356.</div><div class="rule-text">3. Determine Total Cost.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">356.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Apply base cost modifications in any order.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If an ability or instruction allows you to play a card &quot;for [Cost]&quot;, replace the card&#x27;s Base Costs with [Cost].</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If an ability or instruction allows you to &quot;ignore&quot; one or more of a card&#x27;s costs, set the appropriate Base Cost(s) of the card to zero.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If a card allows a player to play a card &quot;ignoring its cost,&quot; its base Energy cost and base Power cost are set to zero.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.1.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If a card instructs a player to play a card &quot;ignoring its Energy cost&quot; or &quot;ignoring its Power cost,&quot; only the appropriate cost is set to zero, and the remaining cost still applies.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.1.b.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Further additional costs and/or cost increases applied in subsequent steps may raise the card&#x27;s Total Cost above zero. Example: Legion Rearguard is a Fury unit that costs 2 Energy and 0 Power and has Accelerate. A player plays Legion Rearguard and is instructed to ignore its costs, but chooses to pay the Accelerate cost. They ignore Legion Rearguard&#x27;s Base Cost of 2 Energy, but the optional additional cost of 1 Energy and 1 Fury Power is added to its Total Cost and must be paid.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">356.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Apply additional costs in any order.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Mandatory Additional Costs</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.2.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Some Additional Costs specified by Passive Abilities on the card being played or another card are Mandatory , and must be paid to complete playing the card. They use the phrase &quot;as an additional cost&quot; and don&#x27;t include the word &quot;may.&quot; Example: A unit has the passive ability &quot;As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit.&quot; To play that unit, a player must kill a friendly unit. See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.2.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">The cost imposed by the Deflect keyword is a Mandatory Additional Cost. See rule 809. Deflect for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Optional Additional Costs</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.2.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Some Optional Costs specified by Passive Abilities on the card being played or another card are Non-Mandatory , and must be paid only if the player made the choice to pay them in step 2. They use the phrase &quot;as an additional cost&quot; and the word &quot;may.&quot; Example: A unit has the ability &quot;As you play me, you may discard 1 as an additional cost. If you do, reduce my cost by [2].&quot; While playing the unit, its controller declares their intention to pay the additional cost in step 2 , applies that additional cost in rule 356.2 , applies the discount granted by paying that cost in rule 356.4 , and discards a card to pay that additional cost in rule 357.2. See rule 363. Passive Abilities for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">356.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Apply cost increases.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">356.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Apply discounts.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Discounts may be applied by the card being played or by any other card or effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.4.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Discounts may say that cards &quot;cost [amount] less&quot; or that one or more of their costs are &quot;reduced by [amount].&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.4.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Discounts that only apply to a component of the cost will be applied when that component is added to the cost of the spell and before any other discounts. Example: Ezreal, Prodigy reads &quot;optional additional costs you pay cost [1] or [A] less.&quot; When playing a Frigid Touch and choosing to pay the additional cost in step 2, as soon as the additional cost is added to the cost of the spell, Ezreal, Prodigy&#x27;s discount is applied to it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.4.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Discounts that apply to a given component of a spell&#x27;s cost may be applied in any order to that component.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.4.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Discounts that apply to the total cost of a spell and not any one component of the cost must be applied after any discount that applies only to a component of the cost.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.4.d.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These discounts may be applied in any order as long as they are applied after component discounts.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.4.e.</div><div class="rule-text">If a discount applies a minimum cost, that minimum applies only to that discount. Example: Eager Apprentice says &quot;While I&#x27;m at a battlefield, the Energy costs for spells you play is reduced by [1], to a minimum of [1].&quot; A player who controls Eager Apprentice and a unit with 7 Might plays Sky Splitter, a spell that costs 8 Energy and says &quot;This spell&#x27;s Energy cost is reduced by the highest Might among units you control.&quot; That player can choose to apply Eager Apprentice&#x27;s discount first, reducing Sky Splitter&#x27;s Energy cost to 7, then apply Sky Splitter&#x27;s discount, reducing its Energy cost to 0. If they applied these discounts in the other order, Sky Splitter&#x27;s Energy cost would be 1.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">356.4.f.</div><div class="rule-text">Discounts can reduce additional costs, including to 0.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">356.4.f.1.</div><div class="rule-text">An optional additional cost was &quot;paid&quot; if the player made the decision to pay it. It doesn&#x27;t matter how much the player actually paid. Example: Clockwork Keeper is a unit that costs 2 Energy and 0 Power and says &quot;As you play me, you may pay [C] as an additional cost. If you do, draw 1.&quot; A player controls a card that says &quot;Units you play cost [A] less.&quot; That player plays Clockwork Keeper and chooses to pay the optional additional cost of [C]. They will draw a card, even though the optional additional cost was reduced to 0.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">356.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Energy and Power costs can&#x27;t be reduced below 0.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">356.6.</div><div class="rule-text">Costs may be Energy costs, Power costs, or non-standard costs. Example: A card reads &quot;As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit.&quot; Killing a friendly unit is an additional cost to play that card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">357.</div><div class="rule-text">4. Pay the card&#x27;s costs.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">357.1.</div><div class="rule-text">In total, pay the combined Energy cost (if any) and Power cost (if any).</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">357.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">During this step, the card&#x27;s controller can use activated abilities with the Reaction tag that Add resources to add Energy and Power to pay the card&#x27;s costs. See rule 164. Rune Pools and rule 429. Add for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">357.2.</div><div class="rule-text">In addition, pay any non-standard Cost summed in step 3 in any order.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">357.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Costs that are replaced with other events by replacement effects are still considered paid. Example: A player plays Cruel Patron, which says &quot;As an additional cost to play me, kill a friendly unit.&quot; They also control Zhonya&#x27;s Hourglass, which says &quot;If a friendly unit would die, kill this instead. Heal that unit, exhaust it, and recall it.&quot; They choose to kill a friendly unit during step 3, but as they pay the cost in step 4, Zhonya&#x27;s Hourglass replaces that unit&#x27;s death. The cost is considered paid, and the player can continue playing Cruel Patron.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">357.3.</div><div class="rule-text">A player may not pay costs during this step that will deterministically result in illegal choices or actions later in this process unless they have no choice. Example: A player plays a card which reads &quot;as an additional cost to play this, you may kill a friendly unit. Give a friendly unit +2 [M] this turn. If you paid the cost, give that unit +7 [M] this turn instead&quot; If they chose to pay the cost, they must choose to kill a unit other than the targeted unit unless they have no choice.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">358.</div><div class="rule-text">5. Check legality.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">358.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Check that all chosen targets are legal.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">358.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Ensure that the outcome of the effect of this card being played would not create an illegal state. Example: Check that a spell&#x27;s execution does not create a state where a Battlefield has Units controlled by 3 different players.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">358.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Ensure that the card has the appropriate permissions to be played at this timing. Example: If the state is Showdown Closed and the card was the one that Closed the state, ensure that it has [Action] or [Reaction]. Example: If the state is Closed and the card wasn&#x27;t the one that Closed the state, ensure that it has [Reaction].</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">358.4.</div><div class="rule-text">If the card, if continued to be played, would create an illegal state, or if a choice or action at this state is illegal, the actions taken in this process are undone and the action is cancelled.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">359.</div><div class="rule-text">6. Finish finalizing this card and proceed with the card&#x27;s category of Play.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">359.1.</div><div class="rule-text">This card is no longer Pending .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">359.2.</div><div class="rule-text">A Permanent leaves the Chain and becomes a Game Object.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">359.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Any passive abilities become active.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">359.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Execute all rules text on the card, from top to bottom.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">359.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If it is a Unit , it enters the Board exhausted at the Location that was chosen.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">359.2.d.</div><div class="rule-text">If it is a Gear, it enters the Board Ready at the player&#x27;s Base.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">359.3.</div><div class="rule-text">A Spell lingers on the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">359.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This card becomes a Finalized Chain Item.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">359.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are other Pending Items on the Chain, then the controller of those Pending Items completes Steps 2 through 5 of Playing Cards for those items before continuing. See rule 327. Chains for more information .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">359.3.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Other players have an opportunity to play Reactions before the resolution of spells. See rule 327. Chains for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">359.3.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Otherwise, execute the game effect of the spell, from top to bottom of the rules text of the card and then place the card in the Trash of the owning player.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-2"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.</div><div class="rule-text">Handling illegal and impossible instructions</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.1.</div><div class="rule-text">The spell resolves even if some or all of its targets are illegal.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.2.</div><div class="rule-text">A target is illegal as the spell resolves if it no longer meets the targeting requirements of the spell, or if it has changed Zones to or from a Non-Board Zone.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.3.</div><div class="rule-text">If a target ceases to meet the targeting requirements while the spell is on the chain, then meets them again, it&#x27;s a legal target. Example: A spell targets &quot;a unit at a battlefield.&quot; A player reacts with a spell that moves the unit to base, then another player reacts with a spell that moves it back to that battlefield, then the original spell resolves. The unit is a legal target.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.4.</div><div class="rule-text">If a target changes Zones to or from a Non-Board Zone and then returns to its original zone, it is no longer a legal target, because it&#x27;s not treated as the same object. Examples: An enemy unit at a battlefield is no longer a legal target if it is no longer an enemy, no longer a unit, or no longer at a battlefield. A unit with 3 or less Might is no longer a legal target if it is no longer a unit or if its Might is greater than 3. Something that&#x27;s exhausted is no longer a legal target if it is no longer exhausted. (It can&#x27;t stop being &quot;something.&quot;) A spell that&#x27;s played from hidden can normally only target its own battlefield or something at that battlefield. A target for such a spell may cease to be a legal target if it moves from the battlefield where that spell was played, even if the spell has no location targeting requirement otherwise.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.5.</div><div class="rule-text">If any of the spell&#x27;s targets are no longer legal, those targets are unaffected by the spell as it resolves. Example: A player plays Void Seeker, a spell that says &quot;Deal 4 to a unit at a battlefield. Draw 1.&quot; The unit&#x27;s controller uses a Reaction to move the unit to their base. Since the unit is no longer a legal target, it is not dealt any damage. Void Seeker&#x27;s controller still draws 1.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.6.</div><div class="rule-text">Instructions that can&#x27;t be followed, either because of illegal targets or other circumstances, are ignored.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.7.</div><div class="rule-text">If all of an instruction&#x27;s Targets become Invalid or Unavailable by the time the spell is finished being played, that instruction will not execute.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.8.</div><div class="rule-text">If an instruction has more than one Target and fewer than all of the Targets become Invalid or Unavailable by the time the spell is finished being played, the instruction will execute, with only the Targets available and valid being operated on.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.9.</div><div class="rule-text">The process for a card&#x27;s choice becoming Invalid or Unavailable is referred to as mistargeting. Example: A spell has the instruction &quot;Deal 2 to a unit at a battlefield.&quot; Before that instruction can execute, the chosen unit is moved to its base. The instruction will not be executed, because it specifies that the unit it chooses must be at a Battlefield, and by the time it attempted to execute, the unit was no longer valid as a choice.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.10.</div><div class="rule-text">It is possible for none of a spell&#x27;s instructions to be executed as it resolves, due to all of them requiring targets to act on and all of those targets becoming Invalid or Unavailable . In this case, the spell has no effect but is still considered played. Example: A player plays a spell that reads &quot;Deal 2 to a unit at a battlefield&quot; with no other instructions, and chooses an enemy unit at a battlefield. They also control a unit with the ability &quot;When you play a spell, give me +1 [M] this turn.&quot; Before the spell resolves, the chosen unit is moved to its base. The spell resolves and its only instruction cannot be executed, but the unit&#x27;s ability still triggers as the spell resolves and gives it +1 [M].</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.11.</div><div class="rule-text">Instructions that can be partially followed are followed as much as possible and ignored otherwise. Example: A player plays a spell that says &quot;Discard 2, then draw 2&quot; If their hand is empty, the instruction to discard 2 will be ignored. They&#x27;ll still draw 2. If they had 1 card in hand, they would discard it and draw 2.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.12.</div><div class="rule-text">If the spell checks information about a target that is no longer legal or a card or permanent whose location, zone, or status has changed such that that information is no longer available, that check returns &quot;null&quot; and all calculations based on it are ignored. Examples: A unit that is no longer on the board is treated as having null Might, null cost, etc. A unit that is no longer on the board has no location, is neither exhausted nor readied, etc. Baited Hook says &quot;[1][C], [E]: Kill a friendly unit. Look at the top 5 cards of your Main Deck. You may banish a unit from among them that has Might up to 1 more than the killed unit and play it, ignoring its cost. Then recycle the rest.&quot; While Baited Hook&#x27;s ability is on the chain, an opponent reacts with a spell that returns the friendly unit to its owner&#x27;s hand. Because the friendly unit is no longer a legal target, it can&#x27;t be killed and its Might is treated as null. Baited Hook&#x27;s controller looks at the top 5 cards of their Main Deck, but can&#x27;t choose any unit from among them.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.12.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If the spell checks information about a target that is legal, or a card or permanent whose location, zone, or status has not changed such that information is no longer available, that information is accessible.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.13.</div><div class="rule-text">A spell or ability that moves something to a different zone as a cost or effect can &quot;look back&quot; at its characteristics before it changes zones.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.14.</div><div class="rule-text">Some instructions may reference Game Objects affected by, or Game Actions performed in, other instructions in a card. The referenced and referencing instructions are called &quot;linked instructions.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.14.a.</div><div class="rule-text">In order for a later linked instruction to execute, its earlier linked instruction must have executed. If the earlier linked instruction is ignored for any reason, the later linked instruction will also be ignored.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.14.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If the Game Action performed in an earlier linked instruction is replaced, this will not affect the later linked instruction.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.e.15.</div><div class="rule-text">A spell or ability that leaves the chain during the process of its resolution will cease further execution of its instructions. This immediately causes the spell or ability to finish resolving.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-2"><div class="rule-id">359.3.f.</div><div class="rule-text">Referents</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.f.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Some information used by abilities is referenced from the source of those abilities, or from one or more targets of a spell or ability. This can usually be recognized by the presence of words like &quot;here,&quot; &quot;my,&quot; or &quot;its.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.f.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Information referenced in an instruction in this way will be checked on execution of the instruction. Examples: A player moves Yasuo, Remorseful to an occupied enemy battlefield and initiates combat there. In reaction to the Yasuo, Remorseful attack trigger, their opponent plays Fight or Flight from hidden targeting Yasuo, moving him back to base. When the attack trigger resolves, &quot;here&quot; is no longer the battlefield where combat is ongoing and the attack trigger mistargets. In reaction to a Yasuo, Remorseful attack trigger, an opponent plays Stupefy targeting Yasuo. When Yasuo&#x27;s attack trigger resolves, it will deal</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-cont level-1"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">damage</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">equal</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">to</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">his</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">current</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">Might</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">of</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">5.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.f.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Some information used by triggered abilities is referenced from the trigger condition of the ability. This information is checked when the trigger condition is fulfilled. Example: Lillia, Fae Fawn reads &quot;when I move from a location, play a 3 [M] Sprite token with Temporary there.&quot; If Lillia moves to a battlefield, her triggered ability will be placed on the chain and it will note the location she moved from when it does so. If she moves to a non-board zone in reaction to the triggered ability on the chain, it will not affect where the Sprite token will be played when the triggered ability resolves.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">359.3.f.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">In the case of a delayed triggered ability, the information is referenced when the triggered ability is created unless specified otherwise.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">359.3.f.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">1 In the case of a linked ability that references information from a linked triggered ability, that information may be referenced from the trigger condition of the linked triggered ability if specified.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">359.3.f.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Some information used by the effect of a triggered ability is referenced from the triggered ability itself, such as &quot;enemy&quot; and &quot;friendly&quot; status. This information is checked on execution of the referencing instruction. Example: Yasuo, Remorseful reads &quot;when I attack, deal damage equal to my Might to an enemy unit here.&quot; Yasuo moves to an occupied enemy battlefield and his attack trigger goes on the chain. In reaction to the attack trigger, the defending player plays a hidden Hostile Takeover and gains control of Yasuo. The triggered ability is unaffected by Yasuo changing controllers, and &quot;enemy&quot; is in reference to the triggered ability itself, so it will resolve with no issue. Example: In reaction to the same Yasuo, Remorseful trigger, say the defending player had instead played a spell that reads &quot;[Reaction]. Gain control of a triggered ability. You may make new choices for it.&quot; They chose the attack trigger. When Yasuo&#x27;s attack trigger resolves, if they didn&#x27;t make new choices for the trigger, the controller of the triggered ability will no longer be an enemy to the targeted unit, so the triggered ability will mistarget and do nothing. If they instead chose Yasuo with the attack trigger, he would be an enemy unit to the triggered ability and so it would deal damage equal to his Might to himself.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">360.</div><div class="rule-text">Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">361.</div><div class="rule-text">An Ability is the structured rules and capabilities of Game Objects or Spells.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">361.1.</div><div class="rule-text">An Ability has multiple structures. Passive Abilities Replacement Effects Activated Abilities Triggered Abilities Delayed Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">362.</div><div class="rule-text">A card can have more than one Ability and more than one type of Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">363.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">364.</div><div class="rule-text">Conditions, rules, constraints, or statements that affect the course of regular play.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">364.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These abilities have a wide variety of formats to recognize. Example: &quot;I get +1 [M] while you have 2 or more cards in your hand.&quot; Example: &quot;Friendly Yordles at my battlefield have [Shield].&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">364.2.</div><div class="rule-text">They can be recognized by being statements of fact.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">364.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Abilities can be conditional.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">364.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Conditional Passive Abilities can be recognized by the occurrence of &quot;if&quot; or &quot;while&quot; as part of the statement of the ability. Example: &quot; While I&#x27;m attacking or defending alone, I have +2 [M].&quot; Example: &quot; If an opponent controls a battlefield, I enter ready.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">365.</div><div class="rule-text">Presence on Permanents</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">365.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Abilities of Permanents are typically only active while on the Board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">366.</div><div class="rule-text">Presence on Card outside of the Board</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">366.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Abilities of cards in zones that are outside of the Board will self-describe their context. Example: The passive ability &quot;Play me only during an opponent&#x27;s turn.&quot; applies in any zone from which that card can be played.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">366.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Abilities can alter the costs of cards as they are played.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">366.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">These apply at all times in any zone from which the card with the ability can be played.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">367.</div><div class="rule-text">Replacement Effects</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">368.</div><div class="rule-text">An ability that alters the application of another game effect or game rule.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">368.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Abilities can be Replacement Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">369.</div><div class="rule-text">Replacement Effects intercede during the execution of a Game Effect and alter its execution.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">369.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A Replacement Effect can usually be identified by the presence of the terms &quot;would&quot; or &quot;instead.&quot; Example: Zhonya&#x27;s Hourglass reads &quot;The next time a friendly unit would die, kill this instead. Heal that unit, exhaust it, and recall it.&quot; This is a replacement effect that alters the execution of any Game Effect that would kill a friendly unit.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">369.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Some Game Actions are themselves Replacement Effects. Example: Burning Out is a replacement effect. Example: Preventing Damage is a replacement effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">370.</div><div class="rule-text">A Replacement Effect can alter the typical flow of play, including other cards&#x27; executions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">370.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Replacement Effects apply to any event or instruction that qualifies for their application. A Replacement Effect will specify the circumstances by which an event or instruction will qualify to be replaced.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">370.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">When a Replacement Effect applies, it replaces the qualifying event with one or more Game Actions or events, or the qualifying instruction with another instruction.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">370.2.</div><div class="rule-text">A Replacement Effect can only be applied once to an event, or to any Game Actions or events that replace that event. Example: A player plays a spell that reads &quot;gear you control become 1 [M] gear units this turn.&quot; They control two copies of Zhonya&#x27;s Hourglass when the spell resolves. If one of those copies is killed, both of their Replacement Effects will be applied. Whichever is applied first, that Replacement Effect can&#x27;t be applied again. When it is applied, it kills its source, which creates an event the other can apply its Replacement Effect to. Once they&#x27;ve both applied their Replacement Effect to the original death event and the event that replaced it, they cannot go any further. At that point, whichever Zhonya&#x27;s Hourglass applied its Replacement Effect last will die.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">370.3.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Game Object has a Replacement Effect that is active in a specific zone, it is evaluated and subsequently applied if it enters that zone before an event occurs that it could replace. Example: A unit that reads &quot;if a unit you control would die, you may banish me from your trash instead. If you do, heal that unit, exhaust it and recall it.&quot; The first unit dies simultaneously with a 1 [M] Recruit token. It does not enter the trash before the Recruit dies, so it will not be able to replace its death.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">371.</div><div class="rule-text">Some Replacement Effects will begin with &quot;once each turn.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">371.1.</div><div class="rule-text">When an event the Replacement Effect could apply to occurs, the player who controls the Replacement Effect may choose to apply it to the event.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">371.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If they do not, it has not been applied this turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">372.</div><div class="rule-text">If more than one Replacement Effect applies to the same event being executed, then the owner of the object being acted on determines the order the Replacement Effects will apply.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">372.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If it is a player being acted on, that player decides the order the Replacement Effects will apply.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">372.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If the affected object is an Uncontrolled Battlefield then the Current Turn Player decides the order the Replacement Effects will apply.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">373.</div><div class="rule-text">If more than one event occurs simultaneously that Replacement Effects could apply to, each event is treated separately and individually for the purposes of Replacement Effects, and Replacement Effects with the same controller are applied in the order of their controller&#x27;s choosing. Example: Two units controlled by the same player die in the same cleanup. That player also controls Zhonya&#x27;s Hourglass. They must decide which event to apply Zhonya&#x27;s Hourglass to first.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">373.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Although these events are simultaneous, the applied Replacement Effects are ordered. If multiple applied Replacement Effects with different controllers would execute simultaneously, they execute in turn order.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">373.2.</div><div class="rule-text">When applying Replacement Effects to events that occur simultaneously, each Replacement Effect may only be applied in one sequence, to any number of events that are qualified to be replaced. Example: Soraka, Wanderer reads &quot;If another unit you control here would die, if it has less Might than me, instead heal it, exhaust it, and recall it.&quot; Soraka dies simultaneously with two 1 [M] Recruit tokens at the same battlefield and two 1 [M] Recruit tokens in base. Soraka has a Guardian Angel attached to her when she dies, which appends &quot;If I would die, kill Guardian Angel instead. Heal me, exhaust me, and recall me&quot; to Soraka&#x27;s rules text. There are several possible ways to order the Replacement Effects being applied to the various events: If Soraka&#x27;s Replacement Effect is applied first, it saves the Recruits at the same battlefield as her but not the Recruits in base. If the Replacement Effect appended by Guardian Angel then saves Soraka, she cannot apply her Replacement Effect to the Recruits in base as her Replacement Effect has already been applied to an event simultaneous with it dying. If the Replacement Effect appended by Guardian Angel is applied first, it saves Soraka and recalls her - then when Soraka&#x27;s Replacement Effect is applied, it can only save the Recruits in base.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">373.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A sequence of Replacement Effects is an uninterrupted series of applications to a set of simultaneous events.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">373.2.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A Replacement Effect that replaces an event or Game Action that is part of another Replacement Effect will not interrupt the sequence of the replaced Replacement Effect&#x27;s application.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">374.</div><div class="rule-text">A Replacement Effect &#x27;s controller is the player that controls the source of the Replacement Effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">375.</div><div class="rule-text">If an event that a Replacement Effect applies to would be modified by a Game Effect , or the results of that event would be modified by a Game Action, the Replacement Effect will inherit those modifications. Example: Treasure Hunter reads &quot;When I move, play a Gold gear token exhausted.&quot; A Replacement Effect that says &quot;if you would play a token gear, play that token and an additional copy instead&quot; is applied to the event of the Gold gear token being played. The additional copy will also be exhausted, as it inherits the &quot;exhausted&quot; modification. Example: Another Replacement Effect says &quot;if you would play a token, draw 1 instead.&quot; The modification cannot apply, so we ignore it. Example: A spell reads &quot;play a ready 3 [M] Mech token. Then do this: Give it Temporary.&quot; A Replacement Effect that says &quot;if you would play a unit token, play that token and a 1 [M] Recruit token instead&quot; is applied to the event of the Mech token being made. The Recruit token enters ready and is given Temporary.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">376.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">377.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated Abilities are repeatable effects with a cost. They follow a process of going onto the chain and resolving, similar to Playing a Card. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">377.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated Abilities are recognized by the presence of a &quot;:&quot; in the text of the card, preceded by a cost and succeeded by an effect. Example: &quot;[2]: Draw 1&quot; is an activated ability. The cost is 2 energy. The effect is to draw 1 card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">377.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Card text will refer to activating Activated Abilities with the word &quot;use.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">377.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If &quot;using&quot; an Activated Ability is part of a trigger condition, that condition is fulfilled when the Activated Ability resolves.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">377.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If an Activated Ability has a condition on &quot;using&quot; it, that condition must be true in order to activate the ability in question. Example: Ultrasoft Poro reads &quot;[E]: Play two 1 [M] Bird unit tokens with [Deflect]. Use this ability only while I&#x27;m at a battlefield.&quot; In order to activate the ability, Ultrasoft Poro must be located at a battlefield.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">377.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated Abilities use the chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">377.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Declare activation of the Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">377.3.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">The ability goes on the chain but has no card to represent it, so players need to take note that it is now a Closed State.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">377.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Proceed with executing the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">377.3.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Follow the steps of &quot;Playing or Activating Abilities&quot; in rule 398 . This ability will become a Pending Chain Item.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">377.3.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Opponents have an opportunity to respond, as appropriate, as if a card was played onto the chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">377.3.b.3.</div><div class="rule-text">If no further action is taken, execute the Activated Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">378.</div><div class="rule-text">The controlling player chooses when and whether to activate an Activated Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">379.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated abilities are present on Game Objects and some Spells.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">380.</div><div class="rule-text">Can primarily be activated while on the Board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">381.</div><div class="rule-text">All Activated Abilities can only be activated on the Controlling Player&#x27;s Turn and during an Open State.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">382.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">383.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities are repeatable effects that happen when a Condition is met.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">383.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities can usually be recognized by the word &quot;when&quot; followed by a game action or event; the word &quot;at&quot; followed by a point in time during the turn sequence; or the phrase &quot;the [Nth] time&quot; followed by a game action or event. Examples: &quot; When you conquer here, you may spend a buff to draw 1.&quot; &quot;At the end of your turn, ready 2 runes.&quot; &quot;The first time I move each turn, you may ready something else that&#x27;s exhausted.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The phrases that identify triggered abilities do not always appear at the beginning of sentences or abilities.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If an ability triggers &quot;the [Nth] time&quot; something happens and that trigger condition is met multiple times simultaneously, the ability&#x27;s controller picks one of those instances to serve as the trigger condition. The ability triggers only once, due to the chosen condition. Example: Wraith of Echoes reads &quot;The first time another friendly unit dies each turn, draw 1.&quot; That ability hasn&#x27;t triggered yet this turn. Two other friendly units die simultaneously (say, due to combat damage). The Wraith&#x27;s controller chooses one of those deaths to trigger Wraith&#x27;s ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">383.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities have a Condition and an Effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Condition follows the When.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The Effect is the Instruction that follows the comma after the Condition.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">The Condition of a Trigger is evaluated after a potentially inciting event has been processed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.2.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Game Object with a Triggered Ability that is active in a specific zone, it is evaluated and subsequently triggered if it enters that zone at the same time that its Trigger &#x27;s condition is met. Example: Immortal Phoenix says &quot;When you kill a unit with a spell, you may pay [1][C] to play me from your trash.&quot; This ability triggers if Immortal Phoenix is in your trash immediately after you kill a unit with a spell, even if the unit you killed with a spell was that Immortal Phoenix.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.2.c.2.</div><div class="rule-text">A Game Object will not be able to successfully be able to evaluate its Trigger Condition , however, if it leaves the zone that its Trigger is active from at the same time that its Trigger is satisfied. Example: Viktor, Leader says &quot;When another non-Recruit unit you control dies, play a 1 [M] Recruit unit token into your base.&quot; This ability triggers if Viktor is on the board immediately after another non-Recruit unit you control dies. It does not trigger if Viktor and another non-Recruit unit you control die during the same game action (for instance, if they are both killed in the same Cleanup due to the damage dealt by Unchecked Power).</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">383.3.</div><div class="rule-text">When a Condition is met, a Triggered Ability behaves like an Activated Ability and is placed on the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Triggered Ability says &quot;you may&quot; as the first part of its Effect , the controller of its source will choose whether or not to place the Triggered Ability on the chain when its trigger Condition is fulfilled.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Triggered Ability contains a cost within instructions, that cost is treated as the base cost of the Triggered Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.3.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">The cost must be paid in order to finalize the Triggered Ability to the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.3.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Costs within instructions for Triggered Abilities are not paid on resolution, unlike costs within instructions for Spells.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.3.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities can be put on the Chain during Closed States or Open States on any player&#x27;s turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.3.d.</div><div class="rule-text">If more than one Triggered Ability is Triggered simultaneously, then the player that controls the Abilities selects the order to place them on the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.3.d.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If multiple players separately control Triggered Abilities that are Triggered simultaneously, then starting with the Turn Player and proceeding in Turn Order , each player orders their Triggered Abilities on the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.3.e.</div><div class="rule-text">If a triggered ability has a conditional statement following the Condition, that conditional statement must be true in order for the trigger to be placed on the Chain. Example: Sona, Harmonious reads &quot;At the end of your turn, if I&#x27;m at a battlefield, ready up to 4 friendly runes.&quot; Her Trigger Ability&#x27;s Condition will be fulfilled in the Ending Step, but the Triggered Ability will only be placed on the chain if she is located at a battlefield when the Condition is fulfilled.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.3.f.</div><div class="rule-text">Some Triggered Abilities will trigger &quot;once each turn.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.3.f.1.</div><div class="rule-text">When the Condition is fulfilled, the player who controls the source of the Triggered Ability may choose to place it on the chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.3.f.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If they do not, it has not Triggered this turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">383.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Some Conditions are commonly used and structured in a way that explicitly defines their use and other properties of the Effect that is associated with it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Play Effects are Triggered Abilities with the Condition that the Permanent that has the Play Effect being played to the board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These are commonly structured as &quot;When you play me…&quot; for Units and &quot;When you play this…&quot; for Gear.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Permanent these effects correspond to is finalized and enters the board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.a.3.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Play Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.a.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Abilities that trigger when another object is played are not considered Play Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.4.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Targeting Effects are Triggered Abilities with the Condition that a Game Object becomes targeted.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These are commonly structured as &quot;When you choose me …&quot; or &quot;When you choose a [Game Object] …&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after a spell or ability that targets an appropriate Game Object is Finalized.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.b.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Although these abilities say &quot;choose&quot; in their Condition , they trigger specifically when an appropriate Game Object is Targeted. See rule 355.6. Targeting for more information on what counts as Targeting.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.b.4.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Targeting Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.4.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Conquer Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit participating in, and successfully Conquering a Battlefield.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These are commonly structured as &quot;When I conquer…&quot; and &quot;When you conquer…&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.c.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This category of Triggered Abilities encompasses only those that are triggered from Units that were present during the Conquer action, or Abilities that reference the player that performed the Conquer action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">383.4.c.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Conquer Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit(s) these effects correspond to are present at a Battlefield when a player gains control of it and gains 1 Victory Point from Conquering.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">383.4.c.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The Conquer Abilities of anything that references the player Conquering is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Conquer and gained 1 Victory Point.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">383.4.c.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If the act of gaining one point from Conquering is negated or replaced in any way, the Conquer Effect will still trigger.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.c.3.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Conquer Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.4.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Hold Effects are Triggered Abilities with a Condition of a Unit being present at a Battlefield during the Beginning phase when a player scores Victory Points from Holding.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.d.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These are commonly structured as &quot;When I hold…&quot; or &quot;When you hold…&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.d.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This category of Triggered Abilities encompasses only those that are triggered from Units that were present during the Hold action, or Abilities that reference the player that performed the Hold action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">383.4.d.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Hold Abilities of Units are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to are present at a Battlefield when a player maintains control of it and Gains 1 Victory Point during their Beginning Phase from Holding.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">383.4.d.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The Hold Abilities of anything that references the player Holding is put on the Chain as a Pending Item when the Condition that the player that controls the triggering source has performed a Hold and gained 1 Victory Point.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">383.4.d.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If the act of gaining one point from Holding is negated or replaced in any way, the Hold Effect will still trigger.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.d.3.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Hold Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.4.e.</div><div class="rule-text">Attack Triggers are Triggered Abilities that trigger when a Unit gains the Attacker designation for the first time during a combat.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.e.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These are commonly structured as &quot;When I attack…&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.e.2.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Attacker designation during Combat .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">383.4.e.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">These triggers will only have their condition checked once per combat, despite a Unit being able to gain and lose the Attacker designation multiple times in the same combat.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">383.4.e.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If the trigger condition contains other requirements besides attacking and if those requirements are not fulfilled when the unit gains the Attacker designation, it will not trigger in that combat.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.e.3.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Attack Triggers.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">383.4.f.</div><div class="rule-text">Defend Triggers are Triggered Abilities that trigger when a Unit gains the Defender designation for the first time during a combat.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.f.1.</div><div class="rule-text">These are commonly structured as &quot;When I defend…&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.f.2.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities are put on the Chain as Pending Items after the Unit these effects correspond to gains the Defender designation during Combat .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">383.4.f.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">These triggers will only have their condition checked once per combat, despite a Unit being able to gain and lose the Defender designation multiple times in the same combat.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">383.4.f.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If the trigger condition contains other requirements besides defending and if those requirements are not fulfilled when the unit gains the Defender designation, it will not trigger in that combat.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">383.4.f.3.</div><div class="rule-text">These Triggered Abilities can be referred to as Defend Triggers.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">384.</div><div class="rule-text">Presence on Permanents</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">384.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Typically active while on the Board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">384.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities of Permanents are only able to have their Conditions evaluated while on the Board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">385.</div><div class="rule-text">Presence on Cards outside of the Board</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">385.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities on cards outside of the Board rely on the Information Level of the zone they are in.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">385.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities outside of the Board will self-describe their context. Example: The triggered ability &quot;When you conquer, you may discard 1 to return this from your trash to your hand.&quot; triggers while the card it&#x27;s on is in the trash, and not anywhere else.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">386.</div><div class="rule-text">Reflexive Triggers</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">387.</div><div class="rule-text">Reflexive Triggers are a type of Triggered Ability that create one or more Chain Items when their condition is met.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">387.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Reflexive Triggers can be recognized by the phrase &quot;Do this:&quot; or &quot;Do one of the following:&quot;.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">387.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;Do this&quot; can be followed by &quot;N times.&quot; The Reflexive Trigger will thus be added to the chain N times when its condition is met.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">387.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Reflexive Triggers will be preceded by their conditions, if any. If no condition is present in the ability then the Reflexive Trigger will always be added to the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">387.3.</div><div class="rule-text">If present, the Condition of a Reflexive Trigger will follow the same format as a Triggered Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">388.</div><div class="rule-text">Reflexive Triggers use the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">388.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A new ability is created and added to the chain as a Pending Item . See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">388.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Reflexive Trigger creates more than one Pending Item it creates them all in order, but does not go beyond the first step of adding them to the Chain. See rule 398. Playing or Activating Abilities for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">389.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">390.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Abilities are a type of Ability whose trigger Condition identifies a specific time during a turn or a specific event that can occur during a specific timeframe.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">390.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Abilities can be any other type of Ability , and contain all of the properties of that type in addition to the properties of Delayed Abilities.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">390.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Triggers are Triggered Abilities that can be recognized by describing a specific time of the turn, or by structuring a Triggered Ability with a specific frame of time as a restriction.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">390.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Replacements are Replacement Effects that can be recognized by specifying the effect they are replacing at a specific time, or &quot;the [Nth] time&quot; in the description of the effect as it resolves.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">390.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Passive Abilities are Passive Abilities that are applicable only during a specified window of time. The time that the Delayed Passive Ability applies will be recognized in the effect that initiates it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">390.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Linked Abilities are Linked Abilities that are generated by another Ability and reference that Ability or Game Objects it affects. Delayed Linked Abilities don&#x27;t necessarily identify a specific window of time, and instead are defined by the Ability they are linked with.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">390.5.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If that Ability affects a Game Object , the Delayed Linked Ability&#x27;s window will be as long as that Game Object is in an appropriate zone.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">390.5.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If the Delayed Linked Ability references the source of the abilities, its window will be as long as the source is in an appropriate zone.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-cont level-1"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">Refl391. Delayed Abilities will resolve or be active just like the ability they augment, but only during the specified time in the effect that created the Delayed Ability. Example: Ravenborn Tome reads &quot;The next spell you play this turn deals 1 Bonus Damage&quot; is a Delayed Passive Ability that passively adds 1 damage to just the next spell played. The next spell is a specific time, and the 1 Bonus Damage is a passive ability. Example: Noxian Guillotine reads &quot;Choose a unit. Kill it the next time it takes damage this turn.&quot; When the chosen unit takes damage is the specified time, and killing it is the condition for a Delayed Triggered Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">392.</div><div class="rule-text">Delayed Abilities are not associated with Units or Gear; they are created by other Abilities or Spells .
