As such they are executed when their condition and/or specified time occurs regardless of whether the source of the Delayed Ability is still on the board or not.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">393.</div><div class="rule-text">Linked Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">394.</div><div class="rule-text">Linked Abilities are a set of Abilities with one or more of the component Abilities referencing the other Abilities in the set.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">395.</div><div class="rule-text">In order for a set of Abilities to be Linked , they must be present in the printed Effect or Rules Text of the same Game Object, or be granted by the same source to another Game Object.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">396.</div><div class="rule-text">Linked Abilities can contain component Abilities of any type.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">397.</div><div class="rule-text">A component Linked Ability that references a Game Object affected by another Ability in the set may only interact with Game Objects affected by the Abilities it is Linked with.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">398.</div><div class="rule-text">Playing or Activating Abilities</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">399.</div><div class="rule-text">Playing or activating Abilities follows the same steps of playing cards.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">400.</div><div class="rule-text">Abilities when added to the Chain become Pending Items until they complete the steps of Playing.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">400.1.</div><div class="rule-text">When an Ability finishes the steps of playing it becomes a Chain Item just like a Spell.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">400.2.</div><div class="rule-text">When an Ability with the [Add] action is finalized it resolves immediately instead of becoming a Chain Item , like a Unit or Gear.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">401.</div><div class="rule-text">1. Activate or trigger the Ability</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">401.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Add a Pending Item to the chain representing the Ability that is either being Activated or Triggered. Notably, although this Chain Item will not have a card representing it, this will create a Closed State. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">401.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If there is currently a game effect being resolved, continue resolving the game effect instead of continuing the following steps.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">402.</div><div class="rule-text">2. Make relevant choices</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">402.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Make all choices required for this ability, such as targets, modes, or other relevant decisions. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">402.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If legal options are not available for an Activated Ability, it is not legal to activate it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">402.3.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are not enough options to make legal choices for a Triggered Ability that has been put on the chain, remove it from the Chain now. It ceases to be a Pending Item but never becomes a Chain Item.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">402.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This is not an Ability being countered.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">402.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are legal options to choose, the ability&#x27;s controller must choose them. They may not decline this stage of playing a Trigger.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">403.</div><div class="rule-text">3. Determine Total Cost</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">403.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Determine the base cost of the Ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">403.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated Abilities will have a cost listed before the &quot;:&quot; in their text.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">403.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Triggered Abilities will typically not have a base cost associated with them when placed on the chain due to their conditions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">403.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Triggered Ability has a cost within instructions (e.g. &quot;[do X] to [do Y]&quot;), the cost is taken as the base cost. See rule 742.1. for more information on costs within instructions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">403.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Apply cost increases and decreases as a result of choices made in the prior step. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">403.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Apply any other cost increases or decreases as necessary. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">404.</div><div class="rule-text">4. Pay Costs</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">404.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Pay costs as determined in the prior step. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">404.2.</div><div class="rule-text">At this stage, players may decline to pay for Triggered Abilities that have incurred a cost. If they do, the ability will cease being a Pending Item and be removed from the Chain. It never becomes a Chain Item.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">404.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This is not an Ability being countered.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">405.</div><div class="rule-text">5. Check Legality</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">405.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Ensure that the Ability&#x27;s targets are still legal.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">405.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Ensure that the Ability&#x27;s effect would not create an illegal state. If it would, resolve in the same way you would resolve a Card that creates an illegal state. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">406.</div><div class="rule-text">6. Proceed with Play</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">406.1.</div><div class="rule-text">This Ability is no longer Pending.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">406.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This Ability becomes a Chain Item.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">406.3.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are other Pending Items on the Chain, their controllers perform the remaining steps of playing now.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">406.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Other players have an opportunity to play Reactions before the resolution of spells. See rule 327. Chains for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">406.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Otherwise, execute the Ability just like a Spell , then clear the Chain Item from the Chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">407.</div><div class="rule-text">Game Actions</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">408.</div><div class="rule-text">Game Actions are actions players may perform at any given time during the game.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">409.</div><div class="rule-text">A player, unless otherwise specified or prompted, may only perform actions on their turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id">410.</div><div class="rule-text">There are two types of Game Actions:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">410.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Discretionary Actions</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">410.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A Discretionary Action is a Game Action that may be performed at any time during a player&#x27;s turn during a Neutral Open State. See rule 307. States of the Turn for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">410.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A player may take any number of Discretionary Actions available to them during their turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">410.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">As long as any conditions, if applicable, are met.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">410.1.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">As long as any costs, if applicable, are paid.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">410.1.b.3.</div><div class="rule-text">As long as it does not result in any forbidden action being taken or game state being created. Example: A player can&#x27;t use the Standard Move discretionary action to move a unit to a Battlefield that&#x27;s already occupied by Units controlled by two other players.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">410.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Limited Actions</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">410.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A Limited Action is a game action that a spell, ability, or circumstance of the turn&#x27;s progression causes the player to perform. A player cannot perform these actions at-will.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">410.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">These actions can only be taken when a player is instructed to do so as the execution of an effect or during their specified occasion during the turn. Example: A player may Draw during the Draw Step of the Beginning Phase of their turn or when instructed to do so by a spell or ability. They can&#x27;t choose to Draw at any other time.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">411.</div><div class="rule-text">Responsibility</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">411.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Game Actions may be the responsibility of up to one player. The player that performs the Game Action is responsible for it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">411.2.</div><div class="rule-text">In the case where a Game Action is performed by procedures of the game and not by any player, that Game Action is not the responsibility of any player.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">411.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Certain rules assign responsibility to players for Game Actions that they are not normally responsible for.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">411.4.</div><div class="rule-text">If an ability triggers when &quot;you&quot; do something, it triggers when a Game Action that you are responsible for occurs. Example: A gear reads &quot;When you move an enemy unit, you may exhaust this to [Stun] it.&quot; It will trigger whenever a move game action that you are responsible for causes an enemy unit to move. If an opponent plays a spell that reads &quot;choose a Battlefield. Each player may move a unit they don&#x27;t control to that battlefield,&quot; and a player that controls the gear chooses to move an enemy unit, their gear will trigger.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">411.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Note that certain Game Actions , specifically Kill, can be attributed to spells and abilities. This attribution is not the same as the responsibility a given player has for the kill game action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">411.5.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Spells and abilities have attribution for game actions, while players have responsibility.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">412.</div><div class="rule-text">Types of Actions</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">413.</div><div class="rule-text">Draw</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">413.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Drawing a card takes a single card from a zone and adding it to the player&#x27;s Hand.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">413.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Unless specified otherwise, drawing takes cards from the Main Deck.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">413.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">413.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Each player draws 1 during the Draw Step of their Beginning Phase.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">413.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The player may draw cards when instructed to do so by other game effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">413.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This action, when instructed, is formatted as &quot;Draw X.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">413.4.</div><div class="rule-text">If a player attempts to draw more cards than are available in their Main Deck , they do the following:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">413.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Draw as many as possible.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">413.4.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Perform a Burn Out. See rule 431. Burn Out for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">413.4.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Draw the remaining cards needed to complete the Draw action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">414.</div><div class="rule-text">Exhaust</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">414.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Exhausting is an action that marks a non-spell Game Object on the board as &quot;spent.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">414.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">To mark it, rotate the card 90 degrees opposite of Readying , so that the orientation of the card is lengthwise in front of you.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">414.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A Unit that is already Exhausted cannot be Exhausted again.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">414.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Unit is instructed to be Exhausted while it is already Exhausted , nothing additional happens.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">414.2.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;Exhausted&quot; is a state for Game Objects on the board that other game effects and rules can reference.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">414.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">414.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Most Exhaust actions will be costs for Activated Abilities or Discretionary Actions. Example: A unit&#x27;s Standard Move exhausts the unit as a cost.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">414.4.</div><div class="rule-text">When Exhausting is listed as a Cost , then the Action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid. Example: A spell says &quot;As an additional cost to play this, you may exhaust a friendly unit.&quot; An exhausted friendly unit may not be exhausted again as the additional cost for the spell, and the additional cost has not been paid.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">414.5.</div><div class="rule-text">In abilities, the Exhaust symbol represents the cost &quot;Exhaust this&quot; or &quot;Exhaust me.&quot; It resembles a card turning sideways.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">415.</div><div class="rule-text">Ready</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">415.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Readying is an action that marks a non-spell Game Object on the board as available for action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">To mark it, rotate the card 90 degrees opposite of Exhausting , so that it is vertically oriented in front of you.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A Unit that is already Ready cannot be Readied again.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Unit is instructed to be Readied while it is already Ready , nothing additional happens.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">415.2.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;Ready&quot; is a state for Game Objects on the board that other game effects and rules can reference.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">415.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A player Readies all non-spell Game Objects they Control during the Ready Step of the Beginning Phase on their turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">415.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may also Ready Game Objects on the board when effects or spells instruct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">416.</div><div class="rule-text">Recycle</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">416.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Recycling cards is the action in which a player takes one or more cards from a specific zone and then puts it on the bottom of the corresponding deck.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">416.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Main Deck cards are Recycled to the Main Deck.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">416.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Runes are Recycled to the Rune Deck.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">416.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Each player Recycles cards to their own Main Deck and Rune Deck , regardless of which player is instructed to perform the Recycle action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">416.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">416.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The player must Recycle cards from the specified zones when instructed to do so by game effects or costs.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">416.3.</div><div class="rule-text">When Recycling is listed as a Cost , the action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid. Example: Vi, Destructive has the ability &quot;Recycle 1 from your trash: Give me +1 [M] this turn.&quot; Each time a player activates the ability, they must recycle 1 card from their trash to pay its cost. If they have no cards in their trash, they can&#x27;t activate the ability, because they can&#x27;t pay its cost.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">416.4.</div><div class="rule-text">When Recycling is part of an effect, a player must Recycle as many cards as possible from the specified zone or zones.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">416.5.</div><div class="rule-text">If 2 or more cards are Recycled to the Main Deck simultaneously, they are placed on the bottom of that deck in a random order. Example: Garbage Grabber has the ability &quot;Recycle 3 from your trash, [1], [E]: Draw &quot; To pay the cost of activating this ability, its controller chooses 3 cards from their trash and places them on the bottom of their Main Deck in a random order.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">416.5.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If 2 or more cards are Recycled to the Rune Deck simultaneously, they are placed on the bottom of that deck in the order of their owner&#x27;s choosing.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">416.6.</div><div class="rule-text">This action, when instructed, is sometimes formatted as &quot; Recycle X from [Zone].&quot; That means to take X cards of the instructed player&#x27;s choice from the relevant zone and recycle them. Example: Dr. Mundo, Expert has the ability &quot;At the start of your Beginning Phase, recycle 3 from your trash.&quot; As that ability resolves, its controller recycles 3 cards from their trash. If there are fewer than 3 cards in that player&#x27;s trash, they recycle as many as they can.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">417.</div><div class="rule-text">Deal</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">417.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Spells, Units, Abilities, and other game effects may Deal Damage to units.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">417.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Assigning Damage during the Combat Damage Step is not Dealing Damage, but will cause Damage to be Dealt when assignment is complete.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">417.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">To Deal Damage to Units, mark the specified amount of Damage on the Unit.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">417.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Damage is marked on each unit separately.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">417.1.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Damage can be Dealt to more than one Unit at the same time.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">417.1.e.</div><div class="rule-text">Valid Damage is a positive integer amount, greater than or equal to 1 Damage .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">417.1.e.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Only Valid Damage is Dealt. Example: A unit has &quot;when I take damage, give me +2 [M] this turn.&quot; A spell is played that Prevents the next 3 damage the unit would take. If a player plays Hextech Ray targeting the unit, it will take no damage and its triggered ability will not trigger. If that player had played Void Seeker instead, it would be Dealt 1 and trigger its ability. Example: A unit is present at Void Gate. A spell is played that Prevents the next 3 damage the unit would take. If a player plays Hextech Ray targeting the unit, it will take no damage - in order to apply the Bonus Damage from Void Gate, the Deal game action would have to occur, and Hextech Ray did not Deal any damage.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">417.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Only Damage can be Dealt.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">417.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Dealing Damage is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">417.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Assigning Damage causes Damage to be dealt outside of being directed to Deal Damage. See rule 454. Combat for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">417.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Dealing can have the intrinsic property of Bonus Damage.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">417.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Bonus Damage is a property granted to the action of Dealing and alters the amount of Damage distributed by this action. See rule 712. Bonus Damage for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">417.6.</div><div class="rule-text">Deal actions can originate from one or more sources.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">417.6.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If a game effect does not specify a source, the game effect describing the Deal action is the source. Example: Void Seeker is a spell that reads &quot;Deal 4 to a unit at a battlefield. Draw 1.&quot; The damage that Void Seeker instructs you to deal is dealt by Void Seeker.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">417.6.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If a game effect does specify a source, then that source is what is considered the origin of the Damage for this Deal action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">417.6.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Units and Spells can be the source of Damage for Deal actions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">417.6.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Abilities can be the source of Damage for Deal actions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">417.6.b.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">When an Ability is the source of Damage for a Deal action, it is in addition to the Spell or Unit that created that Ability. Example: Iron Ballista is a gear that says &quot;[E]: Deal 2 to a unit at a battlefield.&quot; This damage is dealt both by a gear and by an ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">417.6.b.3.</div><div class="rule-text">When a spell or ability specifies a Unit as the source of the Damage for the Deal action, it is not in addition to the spell or ability that specified it. Example: Challenge is a spell that reads &quot;Choose a friendly unit and an enemy unit. They deal damage equal to their Mights to each other.&quot; The damage that Challenge causes to be dealt is dealt by the chosen units, not by Challenge.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">417.6.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Damage Dealt as a result of being assigned during Combat has the Units as its source.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">417.6.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">The Damage assigned, and subsequently Dealt , to attackers has the defenders as the source and vice versa.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">417.7.</div><div class="rule-text">Deal actions can distribute Damage as part of combat actions or non-combat actions.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">418.</div><div class="rule-text">Heal</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">418.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Damage being cleared from Units is Healing.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">418.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If Damage is cleared for any reason it is considered Healing.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">418.2.</div><div class="rule-text">More than one Unit can be Healed at the same time.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">418.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Healing is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">418.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Heal units when game effects instruct them to, or at specific points in the turn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">419.</div><div class="rule-text">Play</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">419.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A player Plays cards by placing them on the chain and queuing them to be finalized. See rule 349. Playing Cards for more information on playing cards. See rule 337. Finalize for more information on finalizing cards.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">419.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">By default, a player can only Play cards from their hand or their Chosen Champion zone.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">419.2.</div><div class="rule-text">This is a Discretionary Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">419.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">As long as a player has the resources to pay the costs associated with the card and legal choices to make for their cards, they may Play cards.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">419.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Game effects may result in cards being played as part of their resolution.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">419.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This treats Play as a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">419.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Treat all steps of Play as normal, except as noted by the game effect creating this Limited Play Effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">419.3.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are no eligible cards to Play when instructed to Play in this manner like this, then nothing happens and resolution continues.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">419.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Some Abilities trigger when cards are played or otherwise check whether cards have been played.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">419.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">These abilities trigger when the act of playing the card has been completed by the resolution of the card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">419.4.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If a game effect prevents the resolution of the card-for example, because the card was countered -the card wasn&#x27;t played and no abilities that trigger on playing cards trigger. See rule 425. Counter for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">420.</div><div class="rule-text">Move</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">420.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Moving is the act of a Game Object moving between two Locations on The Board. See rule 440. Movement for more information on movement.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">420.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Moving is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">420.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only move Game Objects when instructed to do so by Game Effects or costs.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">420.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The Standard Move inherent to Units may also cause Movement. See rule 144. for more information on the Standard Move .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">420.3.</div><div class="rule-text">The Standard Move inherent to Units is a Discretionary Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">420.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Cost is Exhausting one or more Units.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">420.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The Effect is Moving those Unit.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">421.</div><div class="rule-text">Hide</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">421.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Hiding a card is the act of placing a card facedown at a Battlefield you control.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">421.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Hiding is a Discretionary Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">421.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Hidden keyword allows a player to pay a cost to Hide a card any time they have a Hidden card in their hand or Champion Zone and meet the prerequisites. See rule 811. Hidden for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">421.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Cards that are facedown at Battlefields have their gameplay properties and permissions defined by the effect that put them there. Example: Cards that players Hide with the Hidden keyword can be Played for [0] on any subsequent turn as a property of the Hidden keyword.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">421.4.</div><div class="rule-text">If a facedown card would change zones or if the game ends, its owner reveals it to all players. See rule 128. Privacy for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">422.</div><div class="rule-text">Discard</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">422.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Discarding a card is moving it from a player&#x27;s hand directly into their trash without activating or executing its normal rules text.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">422.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The player who is performing the action chooses which cards to send to their Trash , and may use Private Information to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">422.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">&quot;When I am discarded&quot; abilities or other Triggered Abilities that trigger on discarding are executed after discarding has occurred.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">422.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Discarding is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">422.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A player must Discard cards when instructed to do so by game effects or costs.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">422.3.</div><div class="rule-text">When Discarding is listed as a Cost , then the Action must be able to be completed for the cost to be paid. Example: A card has the ability &quot;Discard 2: Deal 2 damage to a unit at a battlefield.&quot; To activate the ability, the card&#x27;s controller must have at least 2 cards in hand and must be able to discard them.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">422.4.</div><div class="rule-text">When Discarding is part of an effect, then a player must Discard as many cards as possible from their hand. If instructed to discard more cards than they have in their hand, further discard instructions are ignored. Example: Undercover Agent has the ability &quot;[Deathknell][&gt;] Discard 2, then draw 2. (When I die, get the effect.)&quot; If Undercover Agent&#x27;s controller has 2 or more cards in hand, they must discard 2. If they have 1 card in hand, they discard 1, and the rest of the discard instruction is ignored. If they have no cards in hand, the entire discard instruction is ignored. Regardless of how many cards they discard, they then draw 2.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">422.5.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot;Discard X.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">423.</div><div class="rule-text">Stun</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">423.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Stunning is the act of selecting one or more Units on the Board and rendering them Stunned.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">423.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Stunned is a binary state. A Unit is Stunned or it isn&#x27;t.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">423.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">A Stunned Unit can not be Stunned again. Example: Eclipse Herald has the ability &quot;When you stun an enemy unit, ready me and give me +1 [M] this turn.&quot; Its controller plays a spell that reads &quot;Stun a unit.&quot; They may choose a unit that&#x27;s already stunned, but if they do, Eclipse Herald will not trigger.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">423.1.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Stunned Units lose the Stunned status at the beginning of the next Ending Step.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">423.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A Stunned Unit does not contribute its might to damage in the combat damage step. See rule 460. The Combat Damage Step for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">423.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">A Stunned Unit must still have damage applied to it equal to, or greater than, its full might value to be killed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">423.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Stunning is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">423.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Stun Units when directed to by Game Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">424.</div><div class="rule-text">Reveal</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">424.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Revealing is the act of presenting a card to all players from a zone that one or more players do not have access to the information of.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">424.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Revealed is a temporary state and is not a zone.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">424.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Other cards, including the card being revealed, can reference the act of being Revealed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">424.1.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Cards remain in the zone they are being Revealed from.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">Example: If a card is being Revealed from the top of a player&#x27;s Main Deck , it is still the top card of that player&#x27;s Main Deck.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">424.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Unless otherwise described, Revealed cards do nothing else beyond become temporarily known information to all players.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">424.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Revealing is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">424.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Reveal cards from Private or Secret zones when instructed to do so by Game Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">424.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">During the course of a game of Riftbound , a player may choose to show Private information to one or more other players. This does not count as revealing and does not trigger any effects that trigger when cards are revealed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">424.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot;Reveal cards from [zone].&quot; Example: &quot;Reveal 2 cards from the top of your Main Deck&quot; would be executed by taking the two cards from the top of your Main Deck, and then presenting them to all players to clearly read and understand at the table. Then, when all players have had a chance to understand the revealed information, return them to the top of the deck in the same order.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">424.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Game Effects can manipulate or modify the cards Revealed while they are Revealed</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">424.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">While cards are Revealed , those cards can be further manipulated, or accessed. They can even have their destination modified for when the Reveal ends. Example: &quot;Reveal 2 cards from the top of your Main Deck. Put one into your hand and Recycle the other&quot; would be executed by taking the top two cards from your Main Deck to the table, and once every player present has had a chance to understand them you would make the selection of one of them to add to your hand. The one you did not select would then be Recycled to the bottom of the Main Deck.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">425.</div><div class="rule-text">Counter</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">425.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Countering is the act of negating the execution, activation, or otherwise playing of a card or ability by a player.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">425.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A card or ability that is Countered does nothing and is cleared from the chain.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">425.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A card that is Countered is not considered to have been played.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">425.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Countering does not refund any costs paid to play a card, activate an ability, or trigger an ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">425.1.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">This includes additional costs.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">425.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Countering is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">425.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Counter cards and abilities when directed to by Game Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">425.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot; Counter [a card or ability on the chain].&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">426.</div><div class="rule-text">Buff</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">426.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Buffing is the action of placing a Buff counter on a Unit . See rule 701. Buffs for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">426.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">A Buff is also an object.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">426.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">To Buff a unit, place a Buff Counter on it if it does not have one already</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">426.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If the unit already has a Buff Counter on it, it does not get another one.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">426.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Units with Buff Counters can still be chosen for actions that Buff units, but will not be Buffed as part of the execution. Example: A spell reads &quot;Buff a unit. Then, if it was buffed this way, draw a card.&quot; It will place a buff counter on a unit that has no buff counter, and then its controller will draw a card. However, if the player chooses a unit with a buff counter on it already, then the card will not be drawn.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">426.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Buffing is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">426.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Buff units when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">426.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot; Buff [one or more units].&quot; e.g., &quot;Buff a unit.&quot; e.g., &quot;Buff a friendly unit.&quot; e.g., &quot;Buff two friendly units at the same battlefield.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">427.</div><div class="rule-text">Banish</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">427.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Banishing is the action of placing a card from any zone to Banishment. See 107.5. Banishment for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">427.2.</div><div class="rule-text">When a card is Banished it is placed directly into the Banishment zone from its origin.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">427.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Banish is not a subset of Kill.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">427.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Banish is not a subset of Discard.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">427.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Cards and effects can refer to cards that were banished by the same object.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">427.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Separate instances of an object or effect banishing cards do not reference other banished cards by objects of the same name or effects originating from cards of the same name. Example: A spell reads &quot;Banish the top card of your Main Deck. When you conquer this turn, draw it.&quot; This card effect allows you to draw the banished card from banishment if a condition is met. If more than one of these effects is played, each one triggers separately. Each card will be drawn separately. If the turn player passes the turn without playing the card, the card remains in banishment indefinitely. If the same player plays another copy of the same spell, banishes another card, and satisfies its condition, they could play the new banished card, but not the original banished card. See rule 393. Linked Abilities for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">427.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Banishing is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">427.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Banish cards or permanents when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">427.5.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot;Banish [one or more permanents or cards].&quot; e.g., &quot;Banish a card from your hand.&quot; e.g., &quot;Banish 2 cards from your trash.&quot; e.g., &quot;Look at the top 2 cards of your Main Deck. Draw one of them and banish the other.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">428.</div><div class="rule-text">Kill</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">428.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Killing is the action of a Permanent going to the trash from the board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">428.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This can be Active or Passive.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">428.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Active Kill is when the action is taken when instructed by a game effect or as a cost for a card or ability.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">428.1.a.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This is referred to as a Kill Instruction.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">428.1.a.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">When a unit with a Deathknell is to be put in the Trash due to a Kill</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">Instruction , it first has its Deathknell added to the chain as a Pending Item. Note the unit&#x27;s location, attributes, and other relevant information to process its Deathknell when finalized before completing this Kill Instruction .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">428.1.a.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Passive Kill is when the action is taken as a result of Lethal Damage or as a consequence for any other state.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">428.2.</div><div class="rule-text">When a permanent is killed it is placed directly in the trash from its place of origin.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">428.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">It is only considered Killed if its origin was any zone on the board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">428.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">This is not a subset of Move.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">428.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Killing is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">428.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Kill units when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">428.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Killing can also be the result of resolving a Cleanup.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">428.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Killing can be attributed to one or more Game Objects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">428.5.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Killed Unit or Gear is said to be Killed by that Game Object.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">428.5.b.</div><div class="rule-text">A spell or ability that contains a Kill instruction is responsible for Killing the Unit or Gear.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">428.5.c.</div><div class="rule-text">When one or more Units is killed due to a Cleanup , that kill action is attributed to the spell or ability that resolved immediately prior to that Cleanup that dealt damage to the Unit or Units . The player responsible for the deal action is responsible for the kill action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">428.5.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Abilities originating from Game Objects that are attributed Kill Actions are attributed in addition to the Game Object that created them. Example: There is a spell that says &quot;Do this twice: Deal 3 to a unit.&quot; Immortal Phoenix is a unit that says &quot;When you kill a unit with a spell, you may pay [1][C] to play me from your trash.&quot; A player plays the spell while Immortal Phoenix is in their trash. The &quot;do this&quot; phrasing means that it has a reflexive triggered ability, which places two triggered abilities on the chain. As each of those triggered abilities resolve, it deals damage to the unit chosen for that ability. If one of these abilities deals lethal damage to a unit, both the spell and its ability are considered sources of the damage, and so both the spell and its ability receive attribution for killing the unit. This means that the spell&#x27;s controller killed a unit with a spell, so Immortal Phoenix&#x27;s ability will trigger.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">428.5.e.</div><div class="rule-text">In order to Kill something &quot;with&quot; a spell or ability, the Kill action must be attributed to the spell or ability, the player must control that spell or ability, and the player must be responsible for the Kill action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">428.6.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot;Kill [one or more permanents].&quot; e.g., &quot;Kill an enemy unit.&quot; e.g., &quot;Kill this, [2]: Draw 1.&quot; e.g., &quot;Kill all gear.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">429.</div><div class="rule-text">Add</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">429.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Adding is the action of putting resources into a player&#x27;s Rune Pool.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">429.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Spells, triggered abilities, and activated abilities that Add resources finalize immediately.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">429.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Priority and Focus will not pass from Add abilities being finalized or resolving, and will resolve before any other outstanding items on the chain are finalized.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">429.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Activated abilities that Add resources and have the Reaction tag can be activated during the playing or resolution of other spells and abilities, any time that those spells or abilities require resources be paid. Example: A player can add Energy and Power through any means before initiating the process of playing a spell. After initiating that process, in the Pay Costs step, they may activate Add Reactions to add Energy or Power to pay costs.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">429.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">When an Add ability is activated in this way, it immediately finalizes and resolves, even during the resolution of spells and abilities.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">429.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Adding is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">429.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Add resources when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">429.5.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot;Add [one or more resources].&quot; e.g., &quot;Add [2].&quot; means &quot;Add 2 Energy.&quot; e.g., &quot;[E]: Add [Y].&quot; means &quot;Add 1 Power of the Order domain.&quot; e.g., &quot;Add [1][G].&quot; means &quot;Add 1 Energy and 1 Power of the Calm domain.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">430.</div><div class="rule-text">Channel</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">430.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Channeling is the action of taking one or more Runes from the top of a player&#x27;s Rune Deck and putting them on the board.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">430.2.</div><div class="rule-text">The Game Effect that instructs a player to channel 1 or more runes may specify the conditions or circumstances under which those runes enter the board. Example: A spell reads &quot;Channel 1 rune exhausted.&quot; As that spell resolves, its controller puts the top rune of their rune deck onto the board and that rune enters the board exhausted rather than ready.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">430.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Channeling is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">430.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only channel runes when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">430.4.</div><div class="rule-text">This action is formatted as &quot;Channel X rune(s),&quot; optionally followed by conditions or stipulations. e.g., &quot;Channel 1 rune.&quot; e.g., &quot;When you play me, channel 1 rune exhausted.&quot; e.g., &quot;Channel 2 runes exhausted. If you couldn&#x27;t channel 2 runes this way, draw 1.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">431.</div><div class="rule-text">Burn Out</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">431.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Burning Out is an action a player must perform if they attempt to move one or more cards from their Main Deck to any other zone in excess of the number of cards remaining in their Main Deck:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">431.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If a player must Draw cards in excess to the number of cards in their deck, they will Draw as many as possible, perform this action, then Draw the remaining amount instructed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">431.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If a player must put one or more cards from their Main Deck in any other zone, such as the Trash , in excess of the number of cards in their deck they will do so as much as possible, perform this action, and then complete the remaining number required by the instruction.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">431.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If an instruction directs a player to look at or reveal cards in excess to the number of cards in a player&#x27;s Main Deck , that player looks at or Reveals as many as possible, but does not Burn Out, then proceeds with the rest of the instruction.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">431.1.c.1.</div><div class="rule-text">If there are insufficient cards among the looked at or revealed cards to perform subsequent actions to the revealed or looked at cards, any further instructions are ignored. This does not cause a Burn Out , even if those instructions would cause those cards to change zones. Reminder: Cards are considered in the zone of origin while being looked at or revealed, in this case the Main Deck .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">431.2.</div><div class="rule-text">To Burn Out , a player does the following in sequence:</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">431.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Performs as much of the prescribed action as possible.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">431.2.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Recycles their trash into their Main Deck. Reminder: When multiple cards are Recycled to the Main Deck at the same time, those cards must be randomized</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">431.2.c.</div><div class="rule-text">Chooses an opponent to gain 1 point.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">431.2.d.</div><div class="rule-text">Completes the remainder of the action that caused them to burn out. Example: A player attempts to draw 1 during their Draw Phase while their Main Deck is empty. That player instead recycles their trash into their Main Deck, randomizing it as normal, then chooses an opponent to gain 1 point, and then draws 1.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">431.3.</div><div class="rule-text">A player&#x27;s Main Deck may remain empty as they Burn Out , usually because their trash is also empty. When they attempt to perform the original action again, it will cause another Burn Out .</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">431.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Unless some effect intervenes, this will result in them burning out repeatedly, giving 1 point to an opponent each time, until an opponent passes the Victory Score and wins the game.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">431.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Points gained after the first Burn Out being processed in sequence cannot be replaced or prevented by any means.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-cont level-1"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">Points gained after the first Burn Out being processed in sequence that cause a player to reach or surpass the Victory Score for their game mode will cause that player to win the game if they also have more points than any opponent.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-0"><div class="rule-id"></div><div class="rule-text">The player wins immediately, without needing to wait for a cleanup to occur.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">431.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Burning Out is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">431.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only burn out when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">431.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Burning Out is a Replacement Effect. See rule 367. Replacement Effects for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">432.</div><div class="rule-text">Double</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">432.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Doubling is the act of increasing a numeric attribute by an amount equal to that attribute&#x27;s current value.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">432.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This creates an effect that modulates that attribute by that specific amount for the duration specified by the Game Effect that instructed the player to perform this action. Example: A unit with 3 base Might and Shield 2 is in combat as a Defender. Since Shield applies, its current Might is 5. A player chooses it as the target for Last Stand, a spell that reads in part &quot;Double a friendly unit&#x27;s Might this turn.&quot; Its current Might is 5, so it gets +5 Might this turn, for a current Might of 10. After combat, Shield no longer applies, but the +5 Might from Last Stand does, so the unit&#x27;s Might is 8.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">432.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Doubling is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">432.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Double when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">433.</div><div class="rule-text">Swap</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">433.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Swapping is the act of increasing one numeric value and decreasing another numeric value on some number of Game Objects such that their values are reversed.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">433.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Swapping creates two different effects that apply to each attribute. One that Increases one value and one that Decreases the other.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">433.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">To accomplish this, determine the difference between these values and then apply an Increase for that amount to the lower value of the two attributes, and a Decrease of that amount to the higher value of the two attributes.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">433.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If both attributes are the same numeric value, Swapping has no effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">433.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Swapping is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">433.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only swap when Game Effects direct them to do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">434.</div><div class="rule-text">Attach</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">434.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching is the act of linking two cards on the board together to combine their effects in some way. This causes one or more cards to become Attached and at least one card to become a Top-Most Card. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">434.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching affects two cards at once.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">434.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">One card will be designated as the one being Attached , and thus become Attached. The other will become the Top-Most Card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">434.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">This is represented by physically laying the Top-Most card on top of the other or others such that all Effect Texts and Might Bonuses are showing, but nothing else from the card or cards Attached.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">434.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">In the situation where there is more than one card attached to the Top-Most card , they should be stacked in such a way that all Effect Text boxes and Might Bonuses are readable. The order of the Attached cards has no bearing on the application of effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">434.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">The Top-Most card has all Effect Text of all cards Attached to it appended to its Rules Text.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">434.1.d.</div><div class="rule-text">The Top-Most Card has its Might modulated by the Might Bonus of all cards Attached to it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">434.1.e.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching one or more cards will cause those cards&#x27; Rules Text to become Inactive for as long as they remain Attached. See rule 716. Attachment for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">434.1.f.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching a card to a new Top-Most Card will cause it to Detach from the card to which it is currently Attached.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">434.1.g.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching a card to its current Top-Most Card will not have any effect.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">434.1.h.</div><div class="rule-text">If a Game Effect instructs a player to Attach a card to its current Top-Most Card , nothing additional happens.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">434.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">434.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Attach cards when directed to by Game Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">434.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Attaching cards does not inherently choose or specify a target. However, Game Effects that Attach cards may do so.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">434.4.</div><div class="rule-text">When a card Attaches to a card, its location becomes the same as the new Top-Most Card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">434.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">This is not a Move.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">435.</div><div class="rule-text">Detach</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">435.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Detaching is the act of unlinking two cards that are currently linked through the act of Attaching . This causes one to cease being Attached , and potentially causes the other to cease being a Top-Most card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">435.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Detaching affects only cards that are currently Attached to another card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">435.1.a.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Game effects that instruct a player to Detach a card that is currently not Attached to anything will do nothing.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">435.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">When one or more cards become Detached , they cease to be in the Attached state.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">435.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">To represent this, these cards should no longer be placed under the card they were previously placed under as Top-Most Card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">435.1.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">If the Top-Most Card no longer has any cards Attached to it after this, it is no longer a Top-Most Card.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">435.1.c.</div><div class="rule-text">The card being Detached has its Effect Text become Inactive and its Rules Text cease being Inactive.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">435.1.d.</div><div class="rule-text">The Top-Most Card ceases to have the Effect Text of the card being Detached appended to its Rules Text.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">435.1.e.</div><div class="rule-text">The Top-Most Card ceases to have its Might modulated by the Might Bonus of the card being Detached.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">435.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Detaching is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">435.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Detach cards when directed to by Game Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">435.3.</div><div class="rule-text">Detaching cards does not inherently choose, or specify a target. However, Game Effects that Detach cards may.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">435.4.</div><div class="rule-text">When a card Detaches from a Top-Most Card , its location is the same as the Top-Most Card from which it Detached.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">435.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If the Detached card was a Gear and this causes it to become present at a Battlefield , it will be Recalled during the next Cleanup.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">435.4.b.</div><div class="rule-text">If the Attached card was Detached because the Top-Most Card changed zones from a board zone to a non-board zone, then the location that the Attached Card will Detach to is the last location the Top-Most Card was at before changing from a board zone to a non-board zone.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">436.</div><div class="rule-text">Predict</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">436.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Predicting a card is the act of looking at a single card from the top of the Main Deck and choosing whether or not to Recycle it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">436.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">When more than one card is Predicted , the Predicting player looks at that many cards and Recycles any number of them.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">436.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The Player who performs the game action may rearrange any cards not Recycled in this way.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">436.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Predicting is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">436.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Predict cards when instructed to do so by game effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-1"><div class="rule-id">436.3.</div><div class="rule-text">This action, when instructed, is formatted as &quot;Predict X.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">436.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If omitted, X is presumed to be 1.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">436.4.</div><div class="rule-text">If a player attempts to Predict more cards than are available in their Main Deck , they will Predict as many as possible instead.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">436.4.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The Player will not perform a Burn Out as a result of Predicting with too few cards in their deck.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">437.</div><div class="rule-text">Prevent</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">437.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Preventing damage is the act of reducing the Damage a set of game objects would take.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">437.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Prevent is an action that interacts with Damage.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">437.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">Prevent appears in statements that define an amount of damage and the source of the damage it will affect, as well as the timespan it will be relevant for.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">437.1.b.1.</div><div class="rule-text">Prevent actions are usually formatted as &quot; Prevent the next X [source] damage that would be dealt to a [unit] this turn.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">437.1.b.1.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The X is referred to as the Prevent Value.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-4"><div class="rule-id">437.1.b.1.b.</div><div class="rule-text">X can be &quot;All,&quot; which specifies an infinite amount of damage.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-3"><div class="rule-id">437.1.b.2.</div><div class="rule-text">Prevent will always apply to the next damage that would be dealt to a unit affected by the Prevent action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">437.2.</div><div class="rule-text">When damage is Prevented , it is replaced with an event where it deals that much damage reduced by the Prevent Value tracked on the Unit specifically.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">437.2.a.</div><div class="rule-text">The damage being dealt as a result of Preventing can never be less than 0, but can be 0. This is equivalent to not dealing damage.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">437.3.</div><div class="rule-text">When damage is dealt this way, reduce the Prevent Value being tracked on the Unit affected by the Prevent action by the prevented amount.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">437.3.a.</div><div class="rule-text">If the Prevent Value is 0 or less, then Prevent is no longer being tracked on the Unit in question, and the effect expires.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">437.3.b.</div><div class="rule-text">The reduced value is the newly tracked Prevent Value.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-2"><div class="rule-id">437.3.c.</div><div class="rule-text">If the Prevent Value is &quot;All&quot; then it remains &quot;All.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">437.4.</div><div class="rule-text">Damage dealt to a Unit that has that all of that damage Prevented is not considered to have been dealt to it at all.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">437.5.</div><div class="rule-text">Damage can still be assigned to Units in combat that are affected by Prevent . The damage dealt as a result of that assignment will be affected by the Prevent action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">437.5.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Damage can be assigned to a Unit up to a value that would be Lethal considering the Prevent Value of all Prevent Actions on a Unit. Example: A unit with 2 [M] is being assigned damage in the combat damage step. The unit has &quot;prevent the first 3 damage I would take each combat.&quot; The unit would need to be assigned 5 damage in order to have lethal damage assigned to it.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">437.5.b.</div><div class="rule-text">No amount of damage is ever considered lethal if the Prevent Value is &quot;All.&quot;</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">437.6.</div><div class="rule-text">Prevent is a Limited Action.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-2"><div class="rule-id">437.6.a.</div><div class="rule-text">Players may only Prevent Damage when directed to by Game Effects.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-plain level-1"><div class="rule-id">437.7.</div><div class="rule-text">Prevent is a Delayed Replacement Effect. See rule 367. Replacement Effects for more information. See rule 389. Delayed Abilities for more information.</div></div>

<div class="rule-row rule-heading level-0"><div class="rule-id">438.</div><div class="rule-text">Replace</div></div>
